The lower level consists of species of Jarul (<i><a href="/wiki/Lagerstroemia_speciosa" title="Lagerstroemia speciosa">Lagerstroemia speciosa</a></i>), Toon (<i><a href="/wiki/Toona_ciliata" title="Toona ciliata">Toona ciliata</a></i>), Jam (<i><a href="/wiki/Syzygium_cumini" title="Syzygium cumini">Syzygium cumini</a></i>), Jalpai (<i><a href="/wiki/Elaeocarpus" title="Elaeocarpus">Elaeocarpus robustus</a></i>) and Glochidion. <a href="/wiki/Liana" title="Liana">Lianas</a>, epiphytes (mostly of orchids, asclepiads, ferns and leafy mosses) and herbaceous undergrowths are abundant.<sup id="cite_ref-BangFlor_126-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BangFlor-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Savannah formations are found in the open, along the banks of rivers and swamps with common tall grasses like Kans (<i><a href="/wiki/Saccharum_spontaneum" title="Saccharum spontaneum">Saccharum spontaneum</a></i>), Shon (<i><a href="/wiki/Imperata_cylindrica" title="Imperata cylindrica">Imperata cylindrica</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Imperata_cylindrica" title="Imperata cylindrica">I. arundincca</a></i>) and Bena (<i><a href="/wiki/Vetiveria_zizanoides" class="mw-redirect" title="Vetiveria zizanoides">Vetiveria zizanoides</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-BangFlor_126-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BangFlor-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Several species of Bamboo are cultivated that are common in Bangladesh including <i><a href="/wiki/Bambusa_balcooa" title="Bambusa balcooa">Bambusa balcooa</a></i> (which is also common in <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a>), <i><a href="/wiki/Bambusa_vulgaris" title="Bambusa vulgaris">B. vulgaris</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bambusa_longispiculata" title="Bambusa longispiculata">B. longispiculata</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bambusa_tulda" title="Bambusa tulda">B. tulda</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Bambusa" title="Bambusa">B. nutans</a></i>; the latter two also being common in the hills of the region.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A number of fish species have become endangered in the area due to <a href="/wiki/Overfishing" title="Overfishing">overfishing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-latif_98-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latif-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> They include Bhoal (<i><a href="/wiki/Raiamas_bola" class="mw-redirect" title="Raiamas bola">Raiamas bola</a></i>), Lakkhya (<i><a href="/wiki/Eleutheronema_tetradactylum" title="Eleutheronema tetradactylum">Eleutheronema tetradactylum</a></i>), Chapila (<i><a href="/wiki/Gudusia_chapra" title="Gudusia chapra">Gudusia chapra</a></i>), Datina (<i><a href="/wiki/Acanthopagrus_latus" title="Acanthopagrus latus">Acanthopagrus latus</a></i>), Rupchanda (<i><a href="/wiki/Pampus_argenteus" title="Pampus argenteus">Pampus argenteus</a></i>), Pungash (<i><a href="/wiki/Pangasius_pangasius" title="Pangasius pangasius">Pangasius pangasius</a></i>), Chhuri (<i><a href="/wiki/Trichiurus_lepturus" class="mw-redirect" title="Trichiurus lepturus">Trichiurus lepturus</a></i>), Ilsha Chandana (<i><a href="/wiki/Tenualosa_toli" class="mw-redirect" title="Tenualosa toli">Tenualosa toli</a></i>), Hilsha (<i><a href="/wiki/Tenualosa_ilisha" class="mw-redirect" title="Tenualosa ilisha">Tenualosa ilisha</a></i>), Faishya (<i><a href="/wiki/Anchovy" title="Anchovy">Anchoviella commersonii</a></i>), Maittya (<i><a href="/wiki/Scomberomorus_commerson" class="mw-redirect" title="Scomberomorus commerson">Scomberomorus commerson</a></i>), Gnhora (<i><a href="/wiki/Labeo_gonius" class="mw-redirect" title="Labeo gonius">Labeo gonius</a></i>), Kata (<i><a href="/wiki/Nemapteryx_nenga" title="Nemapteryx nenga">Nemapteryx nenga</a></i>), Chewa (<i><a href="/wiki/Taenioides_cirratus" title="Taenioides cirratus">Taenioides cirratus</a></i>), Sundari bele (<i><a href="/wiki/Glossogobius_giuris" class="mw-redirect" title="Glossogobius giuris">Glossogobius giuris</a></i>), Bnata (<i><a href="/wiki/Liza_parsia" class="mw-redirect" title="Liza parsia">Liza parsia</a></i>), Koral (<i><a href="/wiki/Etroplus_suratensis" class="mw-redirect" title="Etroplus suratensis">Etroplus suratensis</a></i>) and Kawoon (<i><a href="/wiki/Anabas_testudineus" title="Anabas testudineus">Anabas testudineus</a></i>), as well as <a href="/wiki/Crustacean" title="Crustacean">crustaceans</a> like tiger shrimps.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first eco-park in Bangladesh, <a href="/wiki/Sitakunda_Botanical_Garden_and_Eco_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Sitakunda Botanical Garden and Eco Park">Sitakunda Botanical Garden and Eco Park</a>, was established in 2001 along with a <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical garden</a>, under a five-year (2000–2004) development project at a cost of <span class="nowrap">Tk 35.7&#160;million</span> on 808 hectares (1,997 acres) of the Chandranath Hills in Sitakunda.<sup id="cite_ref-Bangpark_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bangpark-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> The eco-park was established to facilitate <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> conservation, natural regeneration, new plantations and infrastructure development, as well as to promote nature-based tourism to generate income. The park, 405 hectares (1,001 acres), and the garden, 403 hectares (996 acres), under the Bariadhala Range of Chittagong Forest Division, are rich with natural <a href="/wiki/Gymnosperm" title="Gymnosperm">Gymnosperm</a> tree species including <a href="/wiki/Podocarpus_neriifolius" title="Podocarpus neriifolius">Podocarpus neriifolius</a> and species of <a href="/wiki/Gnetum" title="Gnetum">Gnetum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cycas" title="Cycas">Cycas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-coastuddin_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coastuddin-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The park is reported to be able to receive 25,000 visitors in a single weekend.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> With the botanical garden included, the number of visitors can reach up to 50,000.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> According to the <i>International Journal of Biodiversity Science and Management</i>, however, "ignoring the dependence of local people on park resources created conflicts between local communities and the park authority" and "prohibition on the extraction of forest products from the park... make the livelihoods of surrounding villagers vulnerable".<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sitakunda_Upazila&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FCC_Academic_Block.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/FCC_Academic_Block.jpg/220px-FCC_Academic_Block.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="73" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/FCC_Academic_Block.jpg/330px-FCC_Academic_Block.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/FCC_Academic_Block.jpg/440px-FCC_Academic_Block.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="213" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FCC_Academic_Block.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Faujdarhat_Cadet_College" title="Faujdarhat Cadet College">Faujdarhat Cadet College</a></div></div></div>
<p>The educational institutions of the upazila include <a href="/wiki/Faujdarhat_Cadet_College" title="Faujdarhat Cadet College">Faujdarhat Cadet College</a> (founded in 1958), 4 regular colleges (including Sitakunda Degree College founded in 1968), 24 high schools (including <a href="/wiki/Sitakund_Government_Model_High_School" title="Sitakund Government Model High School">Sitakund Government Model High School</a> founded in 1913 and Madam Bibir Hat Shahjania High School founded in 1905), 10 <a href="/wiki/Madrasa" title="Madrasa">madrasas</a>, and 76 junior and primary schools.<sup id="cite_ref-BangSit_33-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BangSit-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> All the secondary schools and regular colleges are under the Chittagong Board of Intermediate and Secondary Education split from the Comilla Board in May 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Dr. <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Shahidullah" title="Muhammad Shahidullah">Muhammad Shahidullah</a> (1885–1969), an eminent Bangladeshi <a href="/wiki/Linguist" class="mw-redirect" title="Linguist">linguist</a>, served as the headmaster of the Government High School from 1914 to 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> On 24 July 1996, members of <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Chhatra_League" title="Bangladesh Chhatra League">Bangladesh Chhatra League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Islami_Chhatra_Shibir" title="Bangladesh Islami Chhatra Shibir">Bangladesh Islami Chhatra Shibir</a> (ICS) in Sitakunda Degree College fought with guns and firecrackers over a minor dispute.<sup id="cite_ref-CanIss_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CanIss-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> On 29 July 1996, two ICS members of the college were abducted and one of them was killed.<sup id="cite_ref-CanIss_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CanIss-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Faujdarhat_Cadet_College" title="Faujdarhat Cadet College">Faujdarhat Cadet College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Military_Academy" title="Bangladesh Military Academy">Bangladesh Military Academy</a> are also situated in this upazila. As of 2001<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sitakunda_Upazila&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, average literacy of Sitakunda Upazila for people of 7 years of age or more is 54.6%,<sup id="cite_ref-census0_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census0-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> while the average literacy of Sitakunda Pourashabha is 53.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-census2_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> There has been an overall growth of 32.9% between 1991 and 2001, which for men was 20.5% and for women 59.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-census3_32-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census3-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> 70,315 people of the Upazila between the ages of 5 and 24 years attend schools, an overall increase of 35.6% between 1991 and 2001, which for men was 28.1% and for women 45.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-census3_32-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census3-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The highest school attendance rate is observed in age group 10–14 years.<sup id="cite_ref-census3_32-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census3-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The health service centers in the upazila include a health complex, an infectious diseases hospital, a railway <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">TB hospital</a>, 11 family planning centres and a veterinary treatment centre.<sup id="cite_ref-BangSit_33-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BangSit-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Railway" title="Bangladesh Railway">Bangladesh Railway</a> set up the hospital at Kumira in 1952 with a capacity of 150 beds. The capacity was reduced to 50 beds in 1994 as some focus was redirected to the Railway Hospital at <a href="/wiki/Central_Railway_Building" title="Central Railway Building">Central Railway Building</a> in Chittagong. Originally built to treat railway employees, the hospital now also treats people from the wider community.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">Malaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dengue" class="mw-redirect" title="Dengue">dengue</a> and other fevers, <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis" title="Hepatitis">hepatitis</a>, as well as respiratory infections including <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> are some of the major health threats.<sup id="cite_ref-shipman_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shipman-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The percentage of disabled in Sitakunda is reported to be the highest in Bangladesh, at 17% compared to the national average of 13%.<sup id="cite_ref-zaka_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zaka-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Banshbaria Union has been declared as 100% sanitized, as all households in the union adopted sanitary latrines,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> while the upazila has only 16% sanitation coverage.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> A survey published in 2006 by the Bangladesh Arsenic Mitigation Water Supply Project found that of the 18,843 <a href="/wiki/Tube_well" title="Tube well">tube wells</a> surveyed, 24.7% were found to be <a href="/wiki/Arsenic_contamination_of_groundwater" title="Arsenic contamination of groundwater">contaminated</a>. Visible signs of <a href="/wiki/Arsenic_poisoning" title="Arsenic poisoning">arsenic poisoning</a> were found in 47 people.<sup id="cite_ref-arsenic_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arsenic-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>National newspapers published in Dhaka including <a href="/wiki/Prothom_Alo" title="Prothom Alo">Prothom Alo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ajker_Kagoj" title="Ajker Kagoj">Ajker Kagoj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Janakantha" title="Janakantha">Janakantha</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Ittefaq" title="The Daily Ittefaq">The Daily Ittefaq</a> are available in Sitakunda, as well as regional newspapers published in Chittagong Azadi and Purbakon. It also has its own local newspapers and a journalist community.<sup id="cite_ref-NMS_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NMS-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, Atahar Siddik Khasru, the president of the local Press Club, went missing on 30 April and was rescued on 21 May.<sup id="cite_ref-Frontiers_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frontiers-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> He was abducted and tortured by unidentified men allegedly on charges of protesting against the harassment of Mahmudul Haq, editor of local magazine <i>Upanagar</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Frontiers_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frontiers-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> On 6 May, about 30 local journalists working for national and local press took to the streets in protest.<sup id="cite_ref-Frontiers_142-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frontiers-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> The other weekly newspaper is <i>Chaloman Sitakunda</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-BangSit_33-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BangSit-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Television channels available in the upazila include satellite television channels like <a href="/wiki/Channel_i" title="Channel i">Channel i</a>, <a href="/wiki/ATN_Bangla" title="ATN Bangla">ATN Bangla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Channel_One_(Bangladesh)" class="mw-redirect" title="Channel One (Bangladesh)">Channel One</a>, <a href="/wiki/NTV_(Bangladesh)" class="mw-redirect" title="NTV (Bangladesh)">NTV</a>, as well as terrestrial television channel <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Television" title="Bangladesh Television">Bangladesh Television</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NMS_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NMS-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The festivals of <a href="/wiki/Maha_Shivaratri" title="Maha Shivaratri">Shiva Chaturdashi</a> in middle of the month of <a href="/wiki/Falgun" title="Falgun">Falgun</a> (end of February) and Chaitra Sankranti at end of the month of <a href="/wiki/Choitro" title="Choitro">Chaitra</a> (mid April) are observed with much fanfare, featuring the largest Hindu fair of the district.<sup id="cite_ref-BangSit_33-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BangSit-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The Sitakunda Upazila Krira Sangstha (Sports Club) is noted for its participation in soccer.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> There are 151 clubs, a public library and two cinema halls in the upazila.<sup id="cite_ref-BangSit_33-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BangSit-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-117"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-117">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Tank</i> is a term that was used in colonial times for a man-made body of water or reservoir (<i>dighi</i>).</span>
